## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics (materials science constitutive modeling / thermomechanics)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which typically appear in thermoelastic and thermoplastic constitutive laws where stiffness, yield/flow stress, and hardening/softening depend on T and nonlinear functions of epsilon.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (T-dependent modulus): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (small-strain elastic response with temperature-dependent stiffness)
- Thermoelastic stress with stress-free strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - (c2 + c3 * T)) (accounts for thermal expansion / evolving reference strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial with thermal coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 + (c4 + c5 * T) * epsilon**3 (moderate strains, anharmonic elasticity, T-dependent tangent modulus)
- Temperature-dependent tangent modulus (rational softening in strain): sigma = ((c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon) / (1 + c2 * Abs(epsilon)) (smooth transition from linear to reduced tangent modulus at larger strain)
- Hollomon-type power-law hardening with T-dependent strength and exponent: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * Abs(epsilon)**(c2 + c3 * T) (plastic-like hardening curve where hardening rate changes with temperature)
- Voce-type saturating hardening with T-dependent saturation and rate: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-(c4 + c5 * T) * Abs(epsilon))) (hardening towards a saturation stress, temperature shifts both level and rate)
- Exponential thermal softening of strength: sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) * exp(-(c3 * T)) (overall stress scale decreases approximately exponentially with temperature)
- Johnson–Cook-like separable strain hardening and thermal softening (no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (empirical plasticity where temperature reduces flow stress multiplicatively)
- Eyring/activation-like stress–strain nonlinearity: sigma = c0 * T * asinh(c1 * epsilon) (rate-process inspired form; stress scale proportional to T with smooth nonlinearity in strain)
- Hyperelastic-like finite-strain surrogate (1D stretch lambda=1+epsilon): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * ((1 + epsilon) - 1 / ((1 + epsilon)**2)) (captures strong nonlinearity at larger deformation; T scales stiffness)
- Smooth elastic–plastic transition via sigmoidal blend: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (1 + exp((c2 + c3 * T) * (Abs(epsilon) - c4))) + (c5 + c6 * T) * Abs(epsilon)**c7 (linear at small strain, transitions to power-law response)
- Temperature-driven phase/transition effect on modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * tanh((T - c3) * c4)) * epsilon (captures abrupt stiffness change near a critical temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd symmetry in strain: many constitutive laws satisfy sigma(epsilon, T) ≈ -sigma(-epsilon, T); use epsilon multiplied by even functions of Abs(epsilon) and T.
- Small-strain limit: as epsilon → 0, sigma should reduce to sigma ≈ E(T) * epsilon; favor forms where d(sigma)/d(epsilon) at 0 equals a T-dependent modulus.
- Thermal softening: increasing T commonly decreases modulus/flow stress; implement via multiplicative softening factors like exp(-c*T) or 1/(1 + (c*T)**n).
- Saturating hardening: sigma often approaches a plateau with increasing Abs(epsilon); use 1 - exp(-c*Abs(epsilon)) or tanh(c*Abs(epsilon)) for saturation.
- Hardening-rate reduction: tangent modulus decreases with strain; rational forms like epsilon/(1 + c*Abs(epsilon)) encode decreasing slope without discontinuities.
- Critical-temperature behavior: phase changes (e.g., glass transition) can create sharp changes in stiffness; model with tanh((T-c)*k) or other smooth step functions in T.
- Thermal strain / shifting reference: stress-free strain can vary with T; include (epsilon - epsilon0(T)) where epsilon0(T) is linear or weakly nonlinear in T.
- Coupled nonseparable effects: hardening parameters may depend on T (exponent or saturation level varying with T); prefer structures where coefficients/exponents are affine in T (e.g., Abs(epsilon)**(c0 + c1*T)).

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `c0*epsilon**c1*exp(-c2/(c3*T)) - c4*(T - c5) + c6*(T - c7)*log(epsilon + c8)`

With c5 = c7 = 331.684..., c8 = 1, this simplifies to:

**GT = c0*epsilon**c1*exp(-c2/(c3*T)) - c4*(T - c5) + c6*(T - c5)*log(epsilon + 1)**

Expanding:
- `c0*epsilon**c1*exp(-c2/(c3*T))` — power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type exponential in T
- `-c4*T + c4*c5` — linear in T
- `c6*T*log(epsilon+1) - c6*c5*log(epsilon+1)` — T*log(epsilon+1) and log(epsilon+1) terms

So GT has these basis function components:
1. `epsilon**c1 * exp(-k/T)` (coupled epsilon-T term)
2. `T` (linear in T)
3. Constant
4. `T*log(epsilon+1)` (coupled term)
5. `log(epsilon+1)`

The key structural features are:
- **exp(-k/T)** dependence (Arrhenius)
- **T*log(epsilon+1)** coupling
- **epsilon**c1 * exp(-k/T)** coupling

Let me check each candidate:

### Candidate 1:
`c0*epsilon**c1 + c2 + c3*epsilon*log(T*c4 + 1) + c5*log(c6*epsilon + 1) + c7*exp(c8/T) + c9*epsilon`

Has `exp(c8/T)` (can match Arrhenius with appropriate sign of c8), but the Arrhenius term is NOT multiplied by `epsilon**c1`. In GT, the exponential is coupled with `epsilon**c1`. Here they're separate. Also has `epsilon*log(T*c4+1)` instead of `T*log(epsilon+1)`. These are fundamentally different functions. **NO MATCH.**

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 2:
`T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*epsilon*log(T*c4 + 1) + c5*exp(c6/T) + c7*log(c8*epsilon + 1)`

- `exp(c6/T)` is not coupled with `epsilon**c2`
- `epsilon*log(T*c4+1)` ≠ `T*log(epsilon+1)` — these are different functions
**NO MATCH.**

Candidate 2 verdict: [NO MATCH]

`c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*log(c6*epsilon + 1) + c7*sin(c8*epsilon + c9)`

`((epsilon+1)**2*(T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon*log(T*c5+1) + c6*log(c7*epsilon+1)) + (T*c8+c9)*((epsilon+1)**3 - 1))/(epsilon+1)**2`

Simplify: `= T*c0 + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3 + c4*epsilon*log(T*c5+1) + c6*log(c7*epsilon+1) + (T*c8+c9)*((epsilon+1)**3 - 1)/(epsilon+1)**2`

`((epsilon+1)**3 - 1)/(epsilon+1)**2 = (epsilon+1) - 1/(epsilon+1)**2`

This introduces rational functions of epsilon. Not matching GT structure. **NO MATCH.**

Candidate 22 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 29:
`T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*epsilon + c6 + c7*epsilon*log(T*c8 + 1)`

Let me look at this more carefully. The GT expanded is:
- `A*epsilon**c1*exp(-k/T)` — Arrhenius coupled with epsilon power
- `-c4*T + c4*c5` — linear T plus constant
- `c6*T*log(epsilon+1) - c6*c5*log(epsilon+1)` — T*log and log terms

Candidate 29 has: `T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon+1) + c5*epsilon + c6 + c7*epsilon*log(T*c8+1)`

Key issue: `epsilon*log(T*c8+1)` ≠ `T*log(epsilon+1)`. These are fundamentally different functions. Also no `exp(-k/T)`. **NO MATCH.**

Candidate 29 verdict: [NO MATCH]

### Candidate 30:
`T*c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**2 + c2*epsilon + c3 + c4*epsilon*log(T*c5 + 1) + c6*exp(c7/T)*Abs(epsilon)**c8`

With epsilon ≥ 0: `c6*exp(c7/T)*epsilon**c8`

This has `exp(c7/T)*epsilon**c8` — this matches the form `epsilon**c1*exp(-k/T)` with c7 negative!

Also has `T*c0*epsilon` and `epsilon*log(T*c5+1)`.

GT needs: `T*log(epsilon+1)` but this has `epsilon*log(T*c5+1)`. These are different. **NO MATCH.**
